  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText10828615436852015142" style="display:none">The third bone-breaking, belly-busting adventure in the series that puts the “funny” back in, um, funny series. That didn’t really work, did it?<br /><br />If you’ve read the previous Skulduggery books then you know what the Faceless Ones are — and if you know what the Faceless Ones are, then you can probably take a wild guess that things in this book are going to get AWFULLY sticky for our skeletal hero and his young sidekick. If you haven’t read the previous Skulduggery books then what are you doing reading this? Go and read them right now, so that you know what all that stuff in the previous paragraph was about. Done? Good. So now you’re on tenterhooks too, desperately awaiting the answers to all your questions, and instead you’re going to have to wait to read the book. Sorry about that.</span>

<div id="review_1104226163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1104226163" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1104226163?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1104226163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13590154223670529424">When I pick up a Skulduggery Pleasant book I know 3 things for sure and certain:<br/>1. I'm going to laugh. <br/>2. There's going to be freaking awesome action sequences. <br/>3. I'M GOING TO LAUGH.<br/><br/>Sarcasm, peoples, it's so gold and good and wonderful it enters my list twice. <br/><br/><b>This is the 3rd book in the Skulduggery Pleasant series and while I loved it, I think I like book 2 the best.</b> There are a truckload of characters in here and, I confess, I get a lot of the secondary characters confused. Their names are aw</span>
  <span id="freeText13590154223670529424" style="display:none">When I pick up a Skulduggery Pleasant book I know 3 things for sure and certain:<br />1. I'm going to laugh. <br />2. There's going to be freaking awesome action sequences. <br />3. I'M GOING TO LAUGH.<br /><br />Sarcasm, peoples, it's so gold and good and wonderful it enters my list twice. <br /><br /><b>This is the 3rd book in the Skulduggery Pleasant series and while I loved it, I think I like book 2 the best.</b> There are a truckload of characters in here and, I confess, I get a lot of the secondary characters confused. Their names are awesome, though. But after a while Scapegrace and Gallow (?) and Bliss and Krav and Fletcher aaaall meld together. Helps that I have a sucky memory. Of course the main characters of Skulduggery, Valkyrie and Tannith and Kenspeckle and Bliss stayed pretty sharp in my mind. <br /><br /><b>Also....it was hilarious, but NOT ENOUGH DIALOGUE!!</b> It really was on the lean dialogue diet. Although there were some spectacular gems.<br /><i><br />“It’s fairly standard. Also, I’m fourteen. Also, your beard’s stupid.”<br />“Isn’t this fun?” Skulduggery said brightly. “The three of us getting along so well.” </i><br /><br />Gloriously funny. <br /><br /><b>OMG AND CAN WE TALK ABOUT THE CLIFFHANGER ENDING?!!</b> I'm wildly furious. I didn't plan to read any more Skulduggery books ASAP (though I love them to death, har, har, pun intended) because I have a towering TBR and <i>need</i> to read OTHER books first. Now? Pfft. Someone get me to the library <i>right freaking now</i>. HOW COULD THE BOOK END LIKE THAT?!! I love these books because they surprise me. Sure the goodies stay standing, but they get bashed and people betray and the action is fierce and full on. <br /><br />I need more. <br /><br /><br /><b>MORE QUOTES OF NOTABLE AWESOME.</b><br /><br />"Well, OK then." He narrowed his eyes. "How about you? Do you have any...romances I should know about?"<br />"Nope. Not one."<br />"Well, good. Excellent. There'll be plenty of time for boys when you leave college and become a nun."<br />She smiled. "I'm glad you have such ambitious dreams for me." (pg. 34)<br /><br />***<br /><br />Skulduggery: "If I knew a little more about how I ended up as a living skeleton with impeccable dress sense, I could give it a try." (pg. 147)<br /><br />***<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13590154223670529424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3481936-damian-dubois?shelf=2015">2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349572144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12096000636240756086">For years these books have been staring me in the face, whether they be at the local bookstore or library, and I felt no real inclination to pick one up to give it a shot. My thoughts were that these were just for kids and simply not worth the time or effort. Something my eight year old daughter might like, but ultimately not for me. Well, boy was I wrong!<br/><br/>I've now read three of these books and each one has been a fun, action-packed and a thrill a minute ride. While some of the names are a little</span>
  <span id="freeText12096000636240756086" style="display:none">For years these books have been staring me in the face, whether they be at the local bookstore or library, and I felt no real inclination to pick one up to give it a shot. My thoughts were that these were just for kids and simply not worth the time or effort. Something my eight year old daughter might like, but ultimately not for me. Well, boy was I wrong!<br /><br />I've now read three of these books and each one has been a fun, action-packed and a thrill a minute ride. While some of the names are a little on the childish side (Ghastly Bespoke, Gruesome Krav) and some of the dialogue just a little too cheesy, the main characters are a joy to spend time with and the storyline just drags you in and urges you to just read one more chapter. And then, at the very end, we get a jaw-dropping cliffhanger that just screams at you to pick up the next book. Now. Like, RIGHT NOW!!<br /><br />I'm definitely looking forward to the next one in the series, Dark Days. Here's hoping that when I go to the library on the weekend there is a copy awaiting me ;)</span>

  <span id="freeText14098129429465847946" style="display:none"><b> actual rating: 4.5/5 stars </b> <br /><br /><b>That's a shame. I'm sure somebody, somewhere, cares. </b><br /><br />This third novel has this series remain fresh and takes it more into a direction that i wasn't expecting but the ending has really kept me interested to continue this series. <br /><br />The hilarious dialogue and banter with in this series pages are always top notch and i love having all the characters just bounce off each other. Also the magic, sarcasm and the adventure make this series something special and make me fall in love with each book i read in this series <br /><br />There are so many different side characters that pop up in this book it's at times getting a little hard to keep up with everyone popping up in this series.   <i>You don't treat me like a child."<br />He smiled. "Of course I do, but you seem to have this ridiculous notion that being treated like a child means to be treated with less respect than an adult. </i>

<span id="freeTextContainer9667307647167635066">I accidentally spoiled myself for the ending of this one, which bums me out, but I'm still going to give it a high rating because I know if I hadn't been expecting it that certain moment would've hit me a lot harder!<br/><br/>5 stars!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15284144300035103924">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>My personal favorite skeleton detective is back - and not quite as snarky as ever. Close enough. <br/><br/> For me this series/book is not at all about the plot, because, let's be honest, it's not the greatest plot and even frustrates me sometimes. The Faceless Ones are starting to grate on my nerves but it's definitely not the worst story I've come across and <i>absolutely everything</i> is made better by the characters. I <i>love</i> Skulduggery and Valkyrie and Tanith. They are one of the best bad ass team</span>
  <span id="freeText15284144300035103924" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />My personal favorite skeleton detective is back - and not quite as snarky as ever. Close enough. <br /><br /> For me this series/book is not at all about the plot, because, let's be honest, it's not the greatest plot and even frustrates me sometimes. The Faceless Ones are starting to grate on my nerves but it's definitely not the worst story I've come across and <i>absolutely everything</i> is made better by the characters. I <i>love</i> Skulduggery and Valkyrie and Tanith. They are one of the best bad ass teams I've come across in a long time. And their banter and constant sassiness...I love it. And the supporting characters too! Not as awesome but for side characters, not bad at all.<br /><br />This Fletcher character intrigues me. Perhaps we shall see more of him? And I'll say this right now: as much as I would love for there to be no romance at all ever in this series and keep everything just the way it is, if Landy decides to do something with Valkyrie and Fletcher and <i>if</i> he continues writing his characters the way he's been doing and <i>if</i> everyone is still their sassy, decidedly <b>not</b> whiny selves, I'll be just fine with it.<br /><br />HOLY FREAKING CRAP. That cliffhanger is, dare I say, Uncle Troll Rick worthy. </span>

<div id="review_131577599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131577599" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2097698-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241012301p2/2097698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131577599?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/2097698-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131577599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7652510452320457901">This is the best and most satisfying Skulduggery book I've read thus far! Granted, I've only read three. Derek Landy just keeps upping it with each book! Never a dull moment! Like the second book, the other characters came into their own, and as cool and awesome as Skulduggery P is, he <i>needs</i> people to get his back. He needs Tanith Low, Ghastly (all taken names are usually quite cool, because Derek Landy is fabulous.), Kenspeckle, and above all, he needs Valkyrie. His team has saved his butt so m</span>
  <span id="freeText7652510452320457901" style="display:none">This is the best and most satisfying Skulduggery book I've read thus far! Granted, I've only read three. Derek Landy just keeps upping it with each book! Never a dull moment! Like the second book, the other characters came into their own, and as cool and awesome as Skulduggery P is, he <i>needs</i> people to get his back. He needs Tanith Low, Ghastly (all taken names are usually quite cool, because Derek Landy is fabulous.), Kenspeckle, and above all, he needs Valkyrie. His team has saved his butt so many times, one finds it hard to imagine what he'd been doing before he met the girl who was formerly Stephanie Edgley.<br /><br />And best of all, Landy makes me panic. I swear, he made me tense up a couple of times throughout the book, because behind all the wit and fantastic plotting and epic fight scenes, he has quietly built a cage of emotional involvement to the people in the book around you. And you let him. So now you're stuck at home, worried sick, thinking, <i>oh crap, oh crap, what if he (or she) dies here?! No! We need him/her!</i> <br /><br />That's right, Derek Landy turns you into a parent. Or perhaps that girlfriend who has just been told that her boyfriend is going to get involved in a gang fight. Or maybe the child of someone who's been admitted to the hospital. Or a pet-owner whose dog/cat is making freaky noises. But I digress.<br /><br />The notion probably seems silly, until you look at it this way: Every series has at least one immortal character. For the Harry Potter series, you knew without fail that Harry, Hermoine and Ron will survive in the end. For the Twilight series, <i>everyone</i> is an immortal character, except the bad guys. For the Artemis Fowl series, you know that Artemis Fowl, Mulch Diggums and Holly Short will pull through no matter what (I'm not so sure about Butler, though, after what happened in the 3rd book). For the Skulduggery Pleasant adventure, it's Valkyrie Cain and Skulduggery Pleasant (notice how his name is behind hers? Nudge nudge, wink wink). But everyone else in the book probably has a date with Death, because Mr Landy can kill them off at any time...just because he can, and probably because he's Irish. And you know in your heart of hearts, he's toying with this idea to slowly drive you nuts with worry. But that's also what makes him awesome. He isn't afraid to wound his equally-if-not-more-incredble characters, make them scream and run (lots of running in his books), and if the story should lead him that way--kill them off. Derek does seem particularly obsessed with inflicting grievous bodily harm on Tanith Low, though... makes one wonder what he has against hot blondes.<br /><br />Anyhew, rambling aside, this book has the most epic final battle so far, and it takes an interesting turn that I almost didn't seen coming, had it not been for my friend who spoiled the ending for me. He shall pay. Also, I have given it some thought, and I'd like Katie Mcgrath to play China Sorrows if ever there's a movie, which I'm sure there will be. And as everyone knows, casting the movie version of a book you've read is an undeniable symptom of obsessive fandom. Oh dear.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7652510452320457901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_647185917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/647185917" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21514123-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546550865p2/21514123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647185917?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/21514123-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21514123-natalie?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647185917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6987527516822075318"><b>"You have a plan, right?"<br/>"I do."<br/>"Can you tell me what it is?"<br/>"We save the world, we all go home."<br/>"That's a good plan."<br/>"I have my moments."</b><br/><br/>If you've read the first two books in this series you know that by the title alone, things are going to get <i>intense</i>. In this, Valkyrie and Skulduggery investigate the murders of several teleporters and find that they're in the midst of a new plot (by new - and old - villains) to bring back the <i>old gods</i> (or "Faceless Ones") to their world, and have to fight to </span>
  <span id="freeText6987527516822075318" style="display:none"><b>"You have a plan, right?"<br />"I do."<br />"Can you tell me what it is?"<br />"We save the world, we all go home."<br />"That's a good plan."<br />"I have my moments."</b><br /><br />If you've read the first two books in this series you know that by the title alone, things are going to get <i>intense</i>. In this, Valkyrie and Skulduggery investigate the murders of several teleporters and find that they're in the midst of a new plot (by new - and old - villains) to bring back the <i>old gods</i> (or "Faceless Ones") to their world, and have to fight to ruin the plot whilst going off whatever information they can find in their wake - it's a good thing that Skulduggery is a detective and has experience with this, otherwise things might be a <i>lot</i> more difficult...<br /><br />I really loved the introduction of Fletcher Renn in this. I felt that he was probably one of the most "normal" characters that have been introduced so far, and he seemed to be the sort of "voice of reason" that you would get from your <i>average Joe</i> (despite the fact that, as a teleporter, he is clearly <i>not</i> average). He was essentially what your average teenager would likely be like if given superpowers; smug, annoying, and crushing on the attractive females nearby, he's also whining about being babysat because of the danger he was in and wanting very badly to <i>not</i> be chased by bad guys for his abilities ;D It was honestly a nice change to have a character that seems so ordinary in comparison to Valkyrie and co. who - whilst all amazing and badass - seem to somehow be able to shrug off every bad thing that happens as nothing more than an inconvenience and whilst it's GREAT to see a 14-year-old female (Valkyrie) be so AWESOME it is a tad unrealistic :P (And yes, I <i>know</i> that's it's a fantasy and I love her regardless, it's just nice to have a more "average" character in this XD)<br /><br />Aside from the introduction of Fletcher, we also had the introduction of a bunch of (not evil - at this stage?) Necromancers, who are keen to ally with Valkyrie and co. to prevent the return of the Faceless Ones, some more tension between Skulduggery and Guild, and one <i>very</i> obsessive detective who <b>hates</b> Skulduggery (and Valkyrie!) and pretty much everything they stand for in the form of Remus Crux, who... to be honest, is rather incompetent from everything I've seen so far. <br /><br />The introduction of Batu as one of the "big villains" in this was super intriguing and a really great plot point, to have someone like him as the mastermind behind the villains' plans was pretty amazing, and I look forward to seeing what other villains come out of the woodworks as a result of what happened in this book (especially with that CLIFFHANGER ENDING). <br /><br />Well... onto book #4! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="6987527516822075318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16328273957193750452">What could be better than a skeleton detective? You read that correctly, the title character, Skulduggery Pleasant, is a skeleton detective with the ability to conjure flames when he snaps his fingers. He’s not your average private eye, to say the least.<br/><br/>We first meet Skulduggery at the funeral of writer Gordon Edgley. He’s the mysterious figure at the edge of the crowd, wrapped up in a trench coat, scarf, and sunglasses, as though he were avoiding the paparazzi. His odd appearance does not go un</span>
  <span id="freeText16328273957193750452" style="display:none">What could be better than a skeleton detective? You read that correctly, the title character, Skulduggery Pleasant, is a skeleton detective with the ability to conjure flames when he snaps his fingers. He’s not your average private eye, to say the least.<br /><br />We first meet Skulduggery at the funeral of writer Gordon Edgley. He’s the mysterious figure at the edge of the crowd, wrapped up in a trench coat, scarf, and sunglasses, as though he were avoiding the paparazzi. His odd appearance does not go unnoticed by Stephanie, Gordon’s clever niece. She is intrigued by this mysterious figure.<br /><br />Gordon was a very successful writer and as he had no family of his own, left the bulk of his estate to Stephanie. This opens a world of possibility to Stephanie, and unbeknownst to her, a world of trouble. Through a series of events, Stephanie ends up at Gordon’s estate, now hers, by herself one night. It is there someone comes looking for key; only this is the kind of someone that smashes windows and doors. Skulduggery to the rescue and so begins their adventures.<br /><br />Recently, Landy was awarded the Red House book prize. Previous winners include Roald Dahl, Jacqueline Wilson, and J. K. Rowling. Not only is he in illustrious company, but the winner is chosen solely by young people’s votes.<br /><br />If you enjoyed the Artemis Fowl series, or the Bartimaeus trilogy, this is one you should check out, as it has the same elements of magic and humor. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780061808340" href="/book/show/9811156-the-faceless-ones">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16212834-hannah-givens?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16212834-hannah-givens?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894210606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7676291138326582116">One of my favorite things about the first book was that Valkyrie embraced the magical world wholeheartedly, with none of the usual dillydallying about whether she actually wanted it or not. So, I don't really appreciate the constant condescension from everyone (except Skulduggery and Tanith) about how she should really go back to her normal life and it'll be so much better for her. But I'm glad to have Ghastly back -- it was super weird that he was hardly mentioned in the second book -- and the </span>
  <span id="freeText7676291138326582116" style="display:none">One of my favorite things about the first book was that Valkyrie embraced the magical world wholeheartedly, with none of the usual dillydallying about whether she actually wanted it or not. So, I don't really appreciate the constant condescension from everyone (except Skulduggery and Tanith) about how she should really go back to her normal life and it'll be so much better for her. But I'm glad to have Ghastly back -- it was super weird that he was hardly mentioned in the second book -- and the plot, while very similar, feels different because there's more of a mystery tone to it and it explores some new types of magic. Plus I really liked the layering of villains, it made for a much more intense listening experience because it was "Who? What? Why?" rather than just "will they defeat him or won't they." And a great ending, shocking but with a potentially-delicious new hook.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7676291138326582116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1946326710" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946326710" />
    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14045412-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575782798p2/14045412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946326710?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/14045412-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11092301-the-faceless-ones">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=g-ya">g-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=sg-f-urban-paranormal">sg-f-urban-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=g-fantasy">g-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14045412-elaine?shelf=f-kindle">f-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946326710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer989964023633266228">Derek Landy is the Irish author of the <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> series that America seems reluctant to discover. It's probably got something to do with figuring out who its audience is and how to target them. My library had books 1-3 and I got to read 1 & 2 before the library lost its license. I had to wait nearly 2 years before my library renewed it for this series, and I doubt I will get to read the rest of the series unless I order them from amazon.co.uk or something. *sigh*<br/><br/>This series is about a</span>
  <span id="freeText989964023633266228" style="display:none">Derek Landy is the Irish author of the <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> series that America seems reluctant to discover. It's probably got something to do with figuring out who its audience is and how to target them. My library had books 1-3 and I got to read 1 &amp; 2 before the library lost its license. I had to wait nearly 2 years before my library renewed it for this series, and I doubt I will get to read the rest of the series unless I order them from amazon.co.uk or something. *sigh*<br /><br />This series is about a tween girl whose beloved, black sheep of an uncle dies under supernatural circumstances. When a detective shows up to investigate, she gets her first glimpse of Skulduggery Pleasant, the skeleton detective. Well that was way back in book 1, and a lot's happened since then. This book is about magical bad guys trying to bring about the return of evil gods which will end the world, and Skulduggery and Co. work to stop it at all costs. Although the names and the skeleton thing may seem silly and childlike, there are an awful lot of murderous, psychopathic characters in this series, both good and evil. Billy Sanguine, for example, is an assassin who can travel through solid objects (walls, underground), has gaping, empty eye sockets and his weapon is a straight razor whose cuts never heal. Yeah.... don't let the cover fool you - this is not a book you will tuck your kids into bed at night with. This series is dark, violent and wickedly funny.<br /><br />As expected, I enjoyed the hell out of book 3 and I hope I can get my hands on the rest of the series without having to wait another two years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="989964023633266228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2066710692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16313186258872261078"><b>Paranormal Fantasy Favorites</b><br/><br/>This was fantastic. By far the best in the series so far. I loved every minute. The characters are great, the humor is hilarious, the story was more intense and took a darker turn, and the action was awesome. By this point I think I will read anything by Derek Landy. <br/><br/><b>Audio Narration</b><br/>Rupert Degas is incredible. One of the very best. He is a narrator not to be missed.<br/><br/><b>Content</b><br/><br/>Just a heads up. The violence was upped pretty hard in this book compared to the previous two from</span>
  <span id="freeText16313186258872261078" style="display:none"><b>Paranormal Fantasy Favorites</b><br /><br />This was fantastic. By far the best in the series so far. I loved every minute. The characters are great, the humor is hilarious, the story was more intense and took a darker turn, and the action was awesome. By this point I think I will read anything by Derek Landy. <br /><br /><b>Audio Narration</b><br />Rupert Degas is incredible. One of the very best. He is a narrator not to be missed.<br /><br /><b>Content</b><br /><br />Just a heads up. The violence was upped pretty hard in this book compared to the previous two from what I remember. This may even be the most violent modern YA book I have read to date. So I would recommend caution if this is a red flag for you before handing this to your kids. Also, the d-word and h-word is used quite a bit throughout the book.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R2IH5S7hOa9k80DrVHOeaWcAebcAWCUYtkPNIdCHeJ19RG43lb/wx8PY9IqjhpS2sV+ef87Vq3/tPYuQHcSKBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h64aD4vgzgr7anNvKDe0ZpcnkNdMUDyeU2pnibfZLrm9iHPdML4HYlxBxw7fwr65QXh3H4LdsvkIFCE4eprcIw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11372781262787140467">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". L</span>
  <span id="freeText11372781262787140467" style="display:none">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". Landy himself was nominated for an IFTA for Best Script. <br /><br />He doesn’t like to brag about all the awards he’s won, such as the Irish Book of the Decade, or the Red House in the UK, or all the other awards that he humbly displays on his mantelpiece. He is also far too modest to mention things like the first book being a Publisher’s Weekly Best Book of the Year, but would like to extend an invitation to Oprah to pop around one day for tea, in thanks for selecting his book for the Oprah’s Book Club Kids Reading List. <br /><br />Derek plays too many video games, reads too many comics, and watches too many movies. He lives in Ireland with too many cats. Occasionally he talks to real people, but only when he absolutely has to.</span>
